{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01UvHmvkbgMzh2bK8TaGnUaV","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"I think I've found the issue! The problem is in the order of initialization in `azx_init_chip`:\n\n**Current order:**\n1. azx_reset (line 1215)\n2. azx_int_clear (line 1218)\n3. azx_int_enable (line 1219)  **<-- Interrupts enabled**\n4. azx_init_cmd_io (line 1223)  **<-- CORB/RIRB initialized**\n\n**Correct order should be:**\n1. azx_reset\n2. azx_int_clear\n3. azx_init_cmd_io  **<-- CORB/RIRB initialized first**\n4. azx_int_enable  **<-- Interrupts enabled after RIRB is ready**\n\nThis is the classic race condition! After a reset, the controller may generate interrupts (especially on resume), but if the RIRB isn't initialized yet, the interrupt handler won't be able to properly handle responses. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_014QCPpVwUd1JnPXBt1a84yk","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Good! Looking at the interrupt handler, I can see that:\n1. At line 1360-1368, it handles RIRB interrupts by calling `azx_update_rirb(chip)`\n2. This expects the RIRB to be properly initialized\n\nThe issue is clear now. When `azx_int_enable` is called before `azx_init_cmd_io`, the controller can start generating interrupts before the RIRB is ready. If an interrupt comes in after `azx_int_enable` but before `azx_init_cmd_io`, the interrupt handler will try to access `chip->rirb` which hasn't been initialized yet, or the RIRB read pointer hasn't The function currently enables interrupts (azx_int_enable at line 1219) before initializing the codec command I/O (azx_init_cmd_io at line 1223). After a resume from suspend, the hardware controller may generate interrupts immediately after reset, but if the RIRB is not yet initialized, the interrupt handler (azx_interrupt) tries to process responses from an uninitialized RIRB, causing the RIRB read/write pointers to get out of sync. This leads to codec communication failures manifested as timeout errors. The fix is to move azx_init_cmd_io before azx_int_enable to ensure the RIRB is ready before interrupts are enabled.
